Yesterday's Financial Conference Held Large Meetings Both Morning and Afternoon: Opinions on the Business Tax Proposal Sent to the Executive Yuan for Reference; Methods for Abolishing Excessive and Miscellaneous Taxes Passed; Two Savings Associations Prevented from Accepting Members; Opium Taxes and Levies Cancelled with a Deadline for Eliminating Addiction; Fourth General Meeting 9

(Nanjing) The fourth general meeting of the Financial Conference was held at 10:30 AM on the 26th, with 134 members present and 7 absent with leave. Kong Xiangxi chaired the meeting and reported the receipt of four official documents: a table of comparative figures for the additional levies on land taxes in various counties submitted by the Shanxi Provincial Department of Finance, and a report on reducing additional land taxes submitted by the Shaanxi Provincial Department of Finance. Discussion began immediately, with Zhang Shouyong, Director of the Second Group, reporting on the review process for the various business tax proposals. The secretary then read out the review opinions and results. The entire matter was of great importance. Wang Chengying and Yang Mianzhong advocated expanding the business tax rate, opposing the review opinions, arguing that Zhejiang Province was currently undergoing construction, and if excessive and miscellaneous taxes were abolished, business tax must be used to offset the loss. Ma Yinchu said that Zhejiang's construction required other methods of compensation, and strongly denounced the harms of the prize-linked savings schemes of the Banque Franco-Chinoise and the International Savings Society, stating that financial authorities should not allow them to operate or should find ways to take them back. The International Savings Society had already collected 60 million yuan, and if it continued, it would greatly affect the national economy. Wang Hantao advocated that the business tax rate should be flexible to suit local conditions, allowing for expansion and contraction, and protecting domestic goods while preventing the intrusion of foreign goods. He suggested forming another committee to review the case in detail. Guan Jiyu said that protecting domestic goods should be done through other means and stated that business taxes in various countries were based on the amount of sales. This type of transaction tax was equivalent to China's likin, an important tax collection, but was extremely harmful to the people and violated the fundamental concept of business tax. He believed that the collection of business tax should classify industries and grade taxes, keeping it simple. He said that the goal of collecting the tax was not to increase the tax rate but to ensure universal collection in order to achieve good results. Chen Changheng said that the tax rate should not be increased and suggested adding the following phrase to the review results: "It is proposed that the Ministry of Finance submit all original proposals and review opinions to the Executive Yuan for referral to the Legislative Yuan as a reference when amending the Business Tax Law." Wei Tingsheng argued that, in the midst of economic depression, he did not support raising the tax rate, and supported passing the original review proposal. Zhang Kailian said that the business tax should be increased to 20 per mille, and Wu Jiantao advocated that all proposals be handed over to the Ministry of Finance for detailed consideration based on local realities. The Chairman said that the stipulation of the business tax rate should be flexible. If various provinces have opinions, the Ministry can allow them to handle it within a possible range. Reducing excessive and miscellaneous taxes naturally required seeking methods of compensation. Currently, agricultural products were not worth much, and farmers were unable to bear the burden. Everyone was striving to revive the countryside and should not increase taxes. The same was true for commerce. As long as merchants could afford it, more taxes could be collected. However, local conditions varied, and local financial authorities should consult with the Ministry of Finance based on actual circumstances. Furthermore, China should not spend according to income but should use income to determine expenditure as a principle, saving where possible. Subsequently, Xu Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance, responded to Ma Leichu's points, stating that the Ministry of Finance would never allow prize-linked savings to profit from taxation. The Banque Franco-Chinoise and the International Savings Society were permitted during the Beijing era and could now be resolved through legislative and administrative means. At this point in the discussion, members felt that the matter of business tax could not be resolved in a short time and expressed their agreement with Chen Changheng's amendment. Representatives from Zhejiang Province were dissatisfied with the review opinions and declared their withdrawal of the original proposal. The Chairman said that this was not possible. As a result, the proposal was amended and passed based on Chen Changheng's suggestion. The original text was revised to read, "All original proposals and review opinions shall be submitted to the Executive Yuan for referral to the Legislative Yuan as a reference when amending the Business Tax Law. If there are any inconsistencies with the articles of the Business Tax Law, amendments or supplements should be requested from the Ministry of Finance for submission to the Executive Yuan for referral to the Legislative Yuan for amendment and promulgation in accordance with the law." Subsequently, the proposal by the Ministry of Finance to reorganize the business tax of various provinces and cities to conform to the original intention of benefiting commerce and increasing revenue was discussed, as were the proposals regarding the stamp tax on title deeds in the Shanghai Special District and the stamp tax on bills of lading for foreign shipping companies. All three proposals were passed according to the review results. After the discussion of the Second Group's review reports, Ma Yinchu reported on the review process for the various proposals of the Third Group. The resolution regarding item A of the fourth part of the Minister's proposal for reorganizing local finances, such as the division of revenue and expenditure between provinces and counties/cities, was passed according to the review opinions and the principles of the First Proposal of the Group. The resolutions regarding items 1 and 2 of the proposal by the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics to determine local budget methods, as well as the various proposals from the Hubei, Anhui, and Shandong Provincial Departments of Finance, were passed according to the review results. Central and local budgets at all levels should be prepared and submitted within the statutory time limit and strictly implemented. The resolution regarding the internal proposal to determine the procedure for reviewing local administrative expenses was passed after amendment according to the review results. Finally, the various proposals reviewed by the Fourth Group were discussed. Zhang Kailian listed various facts from Hunan Province to oppose the review results regarding the proposal by the Hunan Provincial Government requesting the Central Government to issue a clear order that all national tax agencies should continue to entrust the provincial and local governments with close supervision for rectification. Wei Tingsheng said that the Central Government would set up branch offices of accounting and other auditing agencies in various places, making local supervision unnecessary. As a result, according to the review opinions, national tax agencies had no subordinate relationship with provincial and local governments, and the proposal was likely to create confusion with the administrative system and was difficult to establish. The resolutions regarding the proposal to request the Central Government to allocate funds to develop Guizhou's coal and iron mineral resources, the proposal that central and local finances should be mutually supportive to achieve balanced development, the proposal that provincial universities should be converted to national universities or subsidized by the Central Government for improvement, the request that the government order local officials in various provinces to assist in handling the salt affairs reward and punishment regulations, and the request to reduce the expenses of county autonomy to alleviate the people's burden were all passed according to the review results. Finally, Ma Yinchu and nine other members jointly proposed a temporary motion regarding the crackdown on prize-linked savings, requesting that the Banque Franco-Chinoise and the International Savings Society be prevented from absorbing new members, and requesting that the Ministry of Finance send personnel to monitor the funds of these associations. After Kong referred it to members for review, it was submitted to the general meeting for discussion and adjourned at 12:30 PM. The fifth general meeting continued at 2:00 PM to discuss unfinished proposals. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Continued General Meeting in the Afternoon 10

(Nanjing) The Financial Conference continued its meeting at 2:30 PM on the afternoon of the 26th, discussing and passing many proposals. The original proposals are as follows: (1) Proposal on the implementation of methods for abolishing excessive and miscellaneous taxes; (2) Proposal on the land tax clearing plan; (3) Proposal that the abolition of additional local expenses for male head taxes should no longer be compensated by the Central Government; (4) Proposal on maintaining domestically produced goods and raw materials and increasing import taxes on foreign liquor; (5) Proposal that the deed tax rates in various provinces should be lenient to provide relief; (6) Proposal that the fines for deed tax regulations are too heavy and should be amended to reduce them; (7) Proposal that the abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes and similar likin revenue should be compensated by the Central Government; (8) Proposal to strictly prohibit counties from collecting extra levies after the budget is announced to alleviate the people's burden; (9) Proposal that provinces should not re-levy taxes on goods that have already been subject to central unified taxes; (10) Proposal on improving local finances; (11) Proposal on dividing the scope of provincial and county taxes; (12) Proposal by the Ministry of Finance on the unified portion of tax collection agencies; (13) Proposal by the Fujian Provincial Department of Finance on establishing county finance bureaus to implement unified collection and expenditure; (14) Proposal by Liu Kuidu on reforming the tax system; (15) Proposal by Tang Qiyu on unifying the tax collection agencies in various provinces and counties; (16) Proposal by the Beijing and Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureaus to determine the slaughter tax as a type of local tax and amend Article 10 of the Business Tax Law regarding the slaughter tax; (17) Proposal by Liu Kuidu on the slaughter business tax; (18) Proposal by Liu Kuidu on the pawnshop business tax; (19) Proposal by the Ministry of Railways that railway line taxes and levies should be separated and effectively reorganized to facilitate freight transport; (20) Proposal by Chen Changheng et al. that after reducing local land tax surcharges and abolishing excessive and miscellaneous taxes, in order to maintain the balance of local budget revenue and expenditure, the Central Government should coordinate and subsidize local finances; (21) Proposal by the Zhejiang Provincial Department of Finance to re-divide the standards for national and local income; (22) Points to note in the proposal by the Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics of the National Government to determine local budget methods; (23) Point 2 of Part C of the fourth part of the Minister's proposal to reorganize local finances; (24) Proposal by the Henan Provincial Department of Finance that the ratio of administrative expenses to project expenses should be stipulated in the local expenditure budgets at all levels; (25) Proposal to establish a local government accounting system to establish a foundation for reorganizing local finances; (26) Proposal to determine county finances; (27) Proposal to develop local autonomy by submitting all local taxes in the reorganization of land tax and distributing them fairly between the provincial and county levels; (28) Proposal that the land tax increases reported by the land declaration offices in various provinces should be planned as a whole and the security fees of various counties should be handed over to the province for unified collection and expenditure; (29) Proposal to unify the name of land tax and divide land tax into provincial and county taxes; (30) Proposal by the Suiyuan Provincial Department of Finance to request the Central Government to compensate for the deficits caused by the abolition of likin and the current abolition of excessive and petty taxes in Suiyuan Province; (31) Proposal by the Qinghai Provincial Department of Finance to request the Central Government to assist Qinghai Province in strengthening border defense; (32) Proposal that the Central Government should adopt a comprehensive planning and complementary policy for subsequent assistance to various provinces in order to achieve balanced development; (33) Proposal that new projects in various provinces and cities should be reviewed based on local financial resources and implemented in order of urgency; (34) Proposal by the Qinghai Provincial Department of Finance to request the National Government to allocate judicial expenses to reduce land tax surcharges; (35) Proposal to reduce expenditures; (36) Proposal to seek ways to restore the Zhangjiakou-Kulun (present day Ulaanbaatar) transportation; (37) Seeking rural financial relief; (38) Crackdown on private minting of silver and copper coins and private issuance of banknotes to purify the currency administration; (39) Proposal to increase the import tax on wool fabrics separately from the import tax on foreign rayon and rayon fabrics and to set up two factories to prevent loopholes; (40) Financial disclosure; (41) Clarifying the sources of corruption; (42) Improving the financial system; (43) Proposal to set up farmers' silkworm cocoon loan offices to provide relief to rural areas and increase national tax revenue; (44) Proposal to establish a General Editorial Office for the Complete Book of Finance of the Republic of China; (45) Request for the early establishment of a Salt Administration Reform Committee to promote the new salt law to maintain people's food and increase tax revenue; (46) Request for phased and active implementation of the salt law; (47) Proposal to request the Central Bank to quickly set up a branch in Qinghai to facilitate financial activity; (48) Proposal to request consultation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to quickly find ways to recover the privilege of foreign banks to issue banknotes in order to establish the foundation for a unified currency administration; (49) Proposal to include Gansu tobacco in the seven-province tax area to provide relief; (50) In order to vigorously implement the New Life Movement, the Ministry of Finance should quickly formulate regulations for national compulsory savings and compulsory savings for civil servants and soldiers, and the government should order the Central Bank to set up a trust bureau to handle it in order to cultivate integrity and increase the national economy; (51) Proposal to restore the old system of salt administration agencies and abolish the administrative methods concurrently held by audit personnel in order to clarify the system and enhance efficiency; (52) Please issue strict orders to the provinces that the magistrate of each county should quickly train basic local financial talent when handing over the case; (Central News Agency dispatch on the 26th)

Circumstances of the Passage of Important Cases 11

(Nanjing) Many important cases were passed at the Financial Conference on the 26th, both morning and afternoon. The most important ones are summarized below, along with the results of the review.

A. One case submitted by the Executive Yuan for deliberation on the implementation of methods for abolishing excessive and miscellaneous taxes. The review results are as follows, with a slightly modified method proposed: Article 1: The Ministry of Finance shall establish a committee to reorganize local donations, with the Director of the Tax Affairs Department as a member and concurrently as the Secretary and Director. A number of specialized personnel shall be appointed as members and divided into groups to handle affairs. Each group shall cover a number of provinces and, under the direction of the Minister of Finance, handle the following matters: A. Investigate the situation of donations and taxes in various provinces. B. Formulate various reorganization plans. C. Represent the Minister of Finance and make initial contacts and detailed discussions with local financial authorities in various provinces and cities. D. Formulate the types of donations and taxes, tax rates, and collection regulations. E. Any increase in the types of donations and taxes, tax rates, or changes in collection methods in various provinces and cities shall be reviewed by this committee before proceeding with the legislative process. F. [Omitted] G. [Omitted] H. Formulate whether, how, and how much central subsidies should be given to various provinces and cities. Article 2: Each province and city shall establish a Donations and Taxes Supervision Committee to supervise the implementation of the abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes. Except for provinces and cities that have established senates, the Ministry of Finance shall select five to seven fair and reputable individuals from the province or city and request the Executive Yuan to appoint them as members of the Donations and Taxes Supervision Committee. Article 3: The powers of the Donations and Taxes Supervision Committee of each province and city are as follows: (1) Investigate the excessive and miscellaneous taxes and collection situation within the territory. (2) Study the methods for reorganizing donations and taxes within the territory. (3) Present the situation of donations and taxes and the reorganization methods to the provincial and municipal governments and financial departments. (4) Directly present the situation of donations and taxes and the reorganization methods to the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance. (5) Report illegal donations and taxes and illegal acts of personnel of tax agencies within the territory to the Control Yuan. Passed after amendment according to the review opinions.

B. One draft of the Financial Revenue and Expenditure System Law and the Regulations for Reorganizing Local Taxes and Donations submitted by Wei Tingsheng; one report on the abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes submitted by the Rural Reconstruction Society's Twelfth Report. After joint deliberation,

C. Regarding the business tax proposal (another dispatch)

D. Review opinions on the crackdown on private minting of silver and copper coins and private issuance of banknotes to purify the currency administration: China's currency system urgently needs unified reorganization. The Ministry of Finance has already stipulated various reorganization plans. The proposition in this case is based on the regulations of the Ministry of Finance and is extremely practical and feasible. It should be considered established. It is proposed that the Ministry order the provinces, based on the original laws and regulations, to effectively crack down. All mints and bureaus in various provinces should be ordered to stop minting immediately. If there are difficulties in remote provinces, they should report the facts truthfully, and the Ministry will reorganize them separately. Passed according to the review opinions.

E. Proposal for rural financial relief: Review opinions: The fundamental way to revive the countryside is to relieve finance. The proposition in this case is extremely important, and the provisions are comprehensive. It should be considered established. It is proposed that the Ministry of Finance, together with the relevant ministries and commissions, quickly consult and formulate a detailed and specific plan, submit it to the Executive Yuan, and order the provinces to implement it effectively to save the countryside. Passed according to the review opinions.

F. Please consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to quickly find ways to recover the privilege of foreign banks to issue banknotes in order to establish the foundation for a unified currency administration. Review opinions: Currently, there are many obstacles to China's financial administration, which is due to foreign banks not complying with Chinese laws and issuing banknotes. This is just one aspect. Please have the Ministry of Finance consult with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and negotiate with various countries to order all foreign banks in China to comply with Chinese laws in order to uphold sovereignty and benefit finance. Passed according to the review opinions.

G. (1) The Ningxia Provincial Department of Finance proposed that the abolition of excessive and miscellaneous taxes and similar likin revenue should be compensated by the Central Government. (2) The Shandong Provincial Department of Finance proposed to strictly prohibit counties from collecting extra levies after the budget is announced to alleviate the people's burden. Review results: The methods for abolishing excessive and miscellaneous taxes and the preparation methods after the abolition have been approved in another case. The proposal by the Ningxia Provincial Department of Finance to abolish excessive and miscellaneous taxes and be compensated by the Central Government is included in the previous case. The pain suffered by the people from extra levies is even greater than that from excessive and miscellaneous taxes. The proposal by the Shandong Provincial Department of Finance to strictly prohibit counties from collecting extra levies after the budget is announced is in line with financial principles and should be strictly prohibited. Please have the Ministry of Finance submit it to the Executive Yuan and order the provinces to strictly prohibit counties from collecting extra levies. Once verified, they should be severely punished to alleviate the people's difficulties. Resolution: Passed according to the review opinions.

The PingSui Railway Starts Reorganizing Debts: The East Asia Debt is Also a Part, Completely Unrelated to the Nishihara Loans 15

(Nanjing) The Millard's Review said that the PingSui Railway's reorganization of the Japanese East Asia Development Company loan was a prelude to the Chinese government's reorganization of the Nishihara loans. According to the person in charge of the Ministry of Railways, the Japanese newspaper on May 6 reported that an agreement on reorganizing the PingSui Railway's 5.2 million yen loan with the Japanese East Asia Development Company was signed on April 25, which was true. It was negotiated by the PingSui Railway Bureau and East Asia and approved by the Ministry. The Ministry has been actively reorganizing road debts in the past two years, first to improve creditworthiness and second to determine the budget of each road. Since the implementation, the creditworthiness of the railway has improved greatly, which is well known at home and abroad. The PingSui has gradually gained a firm grasp of operations since last year. In order to reduce the burden and sympathize with creditors, methods for reorganizing debts were established early on, and reorganization methods have been signed with forty or fifty creditors. East Asia is one of the creditors and requested reorganization based on the case. The agreement with the Railway Bureau is within the scope of the predetermined plan. As for the terms of the agreement, both the Railway Bureau and the creditor benefit. The PingSui's reorganization of East Asia's debt is part of the PingSui's debt reorganization plan and part of the Ministry of Railways' debt reorganization policy. It is purely a railway affair and is completely unrelated to the Nishihara loans. The Millard's Review mistakenly believed that Chen Youren listed the PingSui East Asia loan as part of the Nishihara loans in his article published in 1918 and published comments based on this misattributed record, which is contrary to the facts. The Nishihara loans did not include the PingSui East Asia loan. There are seven loans and advances in the Nishihara loans: (1) Communications Bank loan, (2) Wireless loan, (3) Jihui Railway advance, (4) Jihei Forest Mine loan, (5) Manchurian and Mongolian Four Roads advance, (6) Gaoxu Jisun advance, (7) War participation loan, all of which have their own history. I don't know why Chen Youren mistakenly included the PingSui Road East Asia loan in it, and the Millard's Review repeated the mistake. (Special dispatch on the 25th)

Official Statement by Administrative Authorities Regarding Transportation and Postal Issues - Japanese Side Confirms Proposal - Our Government Has Not Yet Discussed This 16

(Nanjing) Regarding various issues such as transportation and postal services, rumors have been rampant recently, and newspapers in Shanghai and Beijing have published conflicting reports, leading to differing claims. This makes it difficult for the public to know the truth. A reporter from the Central News Agency, recognizing the importance of this matter, visited the administrative authorities at their official residence on the morning of the 26th to inquire about the actual situation. According to the discussion, regarding the postal issue, the League of Nations Advisory Committee recently resolved on a method for the passage of mail from various countries through Manchuria. This matter is a technical solution for maintaining postal services between administrative organs and is by no means a relationship between governments. However, our country has not yet discussed this matter with Japan, and the reports in various newspapers are not factual. As for the transportation issue, the Japanese side recently proposed research to our responsible officials, but this was not a formal discussion, and it is merely the Japanese side's unilateral opinion. Our government has not yet discussed this matter, nor has it made any specific decisions. The various rumors circulating are all inaccurate. Even if future research between the two sides yields results, it must first be submitted to the central government for comprehensive consideration before a decision can be made. In short, the central government's approach to this matter is based on the principle of not violating the non-recognition of the puppet organization. Otherwise, there is absolutely no room for consideration. (Central News Agency dispatch, 26th)

(Nanjing) Regarding the postal issue in the Northeast, relevant parties are proceeding in accordance with the League of Nations Sino-Japanese Advisory Committee's resolution: "The exchange of mail between League of Nations member states and the Northeast is considered a technical issue, not a relationship between countries, and especially not recognition of the puppet organization." This is to restore normal postal relations within an appropriate timeframe, without any connection to the term "puppet organization." The Ministry of Communications is carefully studying this issue based on the League of Nations resolution. (Special dispatch, 26th)

Foreign Minister Barthou Announces France Is Not Isolated - Contacting Allied Nations - The Door to Disarmament Is Not Yet Closed - But French Policy Remains Unchanged 20

(Paris) Today, the Chamber of Deputies held a meeting to discuss foreign policy. Many figures from the diplomatic community and foreign journalists were present to observe. Foreign Minister Barthou attended and delivered a declaration, which was warmly welcomed by the entire assembly. Barthou first stated that Austria is a pillar of peace in Central Europe, and France's policy has always been to maintain its independence. As for Poland, it is a friend and ally of France. His recent trip to Warsaw has brought Soviet Russia and Poland closer together. Barthou also stated that the Soviet Union's accession to the League of Nations is a major event. Barthou, as a person who cherishes peace, believes that the Soviet Union's accession to the League of Nations will greatly benefit peace. Barthou recounted his meeting with Soviet Foreign Commissar Litvinov in Geneva, saying that he had discussed the Soviet Union's accession to the League of Nations with Litvinov. However, regarding the Soviet Union's request to become a permanent member of the League of Nations Executive Council, it seems too early to say what attitude France will take. Barthou then recounted his visits to Czechoslovakia and Poland, saying that the warm hospitality of the people of both countries was unforgettable. His trip to Warsaw consolidated the alliance treaty between France and Poland in 1921. He will soon travel to Romania and Yugoslavia, and even if there are disagreements between them, they can be eliminated through this. He will meet with Turkish Foreign Minister Rushdi this Saturday. This shows that France's policy is to connect with the emotions of all parties.

Regarding the issue of disarmament, Barthou stated that the policies pursued by previous cabinets are still being followed, namely disarmament under conditions of security and seeking equality in armaments. However, France cannot ignore military groups outside of Germany's formal army, and as long as Germany's rearmament actions do not stop for a day, France cannot recognize disarmament for a day. France's reply to the United Kingdom on April 17th stated that France has always believed that the Disarmament Conference should take disarmament as its final result. As for rearmament that is contrary to peace treaties, it should not be recognized by the Disarmament Conference. But in any case, the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference have not closed their doors. The French government has always supported peace and has always been loyal to the League of Nations.

Regarding the Saarland vote next year, Barthou said that the freedom of voters must be absolutely respected. During the discussion in Geneva, any measures that would endanger Saarland residents to retaliation after voting were resolutely rejected. France has not abandoned any of the rights it has obtained from treaties regarding the Saarland issue, which is deeply gratifying. Barthou said that in Geneva, he declared to Aloisi, the chairman of the special committee on the Saarland issue, that effective safeguards must be taken for the Saarland residents' vote. Germany's empty guarantees of freedom of voting, even if they are formal declarations, are insufficient. At that time, Aloisi and the special committee drafted a method that they considered acceptable, namely, "France and Germany are willing to recognize all measures that the League of Nations can take to protect Saarland residents." However, the German government was unwilling to accept this method, which is regrettable.

Barthou concluded by saying that none of the French people enjoy fighting. The French are doing everything they can to avoid war, and he believes that war can be avoided. The French will always be consistent towards friends and allies. It is not impossible for France and Italy to establish a friendly agreement, and its relationship with the United Kingdom has not cooled down. At this time, someone raised questions about France's international relations. Barthou replied that France is not in an isolated position. At this point, almost all the members of the audience applauded, including the Socialist Party. The Chamber of Deputies then decided to postpone the questioning on foreign policy until the Foreign Minister returned from Geneva, as he would have to go there soon. The meeting then adjourned. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

Preparing for the Disarmament Conference - Foreign Ministers of Various Countries Go Together 22

(Geneva) Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, arrived here this morning. While talking to people in the Disarmament Conference lounge today, Henderson declared that he did not intend to put forward any new proposals at this session of the conference. In his opinion, only the countries attending the Disarmament Conference, especially those most closely related to the disarmament issue, could clearly state their intentions and, when necessary, put forward new proposals. It was rumored that Henderson favored returning the entire dossier on the disarmament issue to the League of Nations Executive Council as an ending. Henderson denied this rumor again today. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

(London) Although England and France are only separated by a narrow strip of water, their concepts of security are completely different. Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, spoke to a special reporter from the News Chronicle after returning to England from Paris about two conflicting views on the Disarmament Conference. First, in Henderson's view, the best way to get Germany to return to Geneva is for the entire General Committee of the Disarmament Conference to reiterate the declaration of December 11, 1932, in which the five major powers allowed Germany to obtain equal rights to armaments within the scope of security. Second, Henderson is most opposed to transferring the negotiations on the disarmament issue to the League of Nations Executive Council. He said, "I don't see any benefit to this method. It is undoubtedly true that Germany cannot attend the League of Nations Executive Council. As far as the interests of small countries are concerned, they have more representatives on the main disarmament committee than on the League of Nations Executive Council. As for the major powers, their opinions are divided, and as a result, all progress has been inhibited so far. It is difficult to hope that they will be able to cooperate more harmoniously and move forward more bravely on the League of Nations Executive Council than in normal disarmament negotiations. Furthermore, in the event of failure, public opinion will blame the League of Nations itself, rather than the politicians representing the country." The principle that the Disarmament Conference should be based on the five-power declaration of December 11, 1932, is to give Germany and other countries whose armaments have been reduced by treaty, in principle, the right to armament equality within a security system suitable for all countries. Germany then returned to the Disarmament Conference. (Havas dispatch, 26th)

(Paris) The General Committee of the Disarmament Conference will meet in Geneva on the 29th of this month. The United States will still send Davis to attend as an observer. Davis arrived here today from the United States. Henderson, Chairman of the Disarmament Conference, also arrived here from London. Henderson and Davis traveled to Geneva together by train this evening. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

(Paris) British Foreign Secretary Simon is scheduled to arrive here from London on Sunday. He will most likely travel to Geneva with Foreign Minister Barthou to attend the General Committee meeting of the Disarmament Conference on Tuesday of next week. (Havas dispatch, 25th)

So far, including the Netherlands, there are already 13 countries supporting it. There is no reply from Czechoslovakia regarding the League of Nations' proposal. Czechoslovakia is one of the largest suppliers of arms required by South American countries. (Reuters dispatch, 26th)

Bulgaria Becomes a Hotbed of Global Narcotics Production: Influx of Materials Has Increased Greatly in Recent Years; Also Has a Large-Scale Transportation Organization; US Representative Addresses League of Nations Opium Advisory Committee 29

(Geneva) Today, US Representative Fuller, at a meeting of the Opium Advisory Committee, stated the inside story of Bulgaria's opium and narcotics trafficking. Fuller quoted Cairo Police Chief Russell as saying that Bulgaria is still one of the major sources of narcotics production in Europe, attracting villains from all over the world. In 1930, Bulgaria imported few materials for manufacturing narcotics. However, by 1933, the imported materials were sufficient to manufacture twelve times the amount of narcotics needed for legitimate purposes worldwide. Bulgaria currently has the most well-organized smuggling organization in the world, and a former Sofia police chief is the owner of a narcotics factory, while another Minister of Health also runs this business, it is said. (Reuter, 25th)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Opium Advisory Committee held a meeting today. Austrian representative Sulzer chaired the meeting, and US Representative Fuller reported various narcotics figures to prove that the amount of anhydrous acetic acid manufactured in France and Germany and imported into Bulgaria has greatly increased. This anhydrous acetic acid can be used to manufacture as much as 6,000 kilograms of heroin, while the legitimate demand for heroin worldwide is only 1,500 kilograms. Canadian representative Sharman reported that Bulgaria's opium production in 1931 was 4,000 kilograms, which increased to 45,000 kilograms in 1932, and then increased by another 20,000 kilograms in 1933 to as much as 65,000 kilograms. Egyptian representative Russell explained that farmers in the Macedonian region of Bulgaria have switched to growing poppies because they cannot sell their tobacco and wheat. Neighboring countries, seeing the benefits, may follow suit, thus Macedonia has become a hotbed of opium and narcotics in Europe and the world. Italian representative Cavalchini hoped that the Bulgarian government would take strict measures. The Bulgarian representative then spoke, saying that since the establishment of the new Bulgarian government, his duties in this matter have been removed. However, the new government has decided to strictly fulfill its obligations and will take the measures required by the Advisory Committee, he assured. US Representative Fuller then spoke again, requesting France, Germany, and Bulgaria to submit reports on the export and import of anhydrous acetic acid. The committee subsequently passed a draft resolution stating that Article 15 of the International Convention (the International Convention for Limiting the Manufacture and Regulating the Distribution of Narcotics, signed on July 13, 1931) stipulates the establishment of a special administrative body to handle narcotics issues. Governments of all countries should submit reports to the Advisory Committee on the measures taken to establish this body and the methods to prevent the illegal sale of narcotics. The governments of all countries are also requested to collect information and report to the committee on the drug resistance situation of various international and domestic anti-narcotics groups and missionary organizations. (Havas, 25th)

(Geneva) After the Opium Advisory Committee released shocking news yesterday about Bulgaria's illegal manufacturing and sale of opium and narcotics, the Bulgarian representative declared today that the new government has dismissed the public health official mentioned by Egyptian Police Chief Russell. The new government has asked the League of Nations to provide information at any time so that it can quickly and seriously deal with the buying and selling of drugs, it is said. (Reuter, 26th)

Labor Unrest in the United States Rises and Falls: Truck Drivers' Strike Ends; Situation in the Electrical Industry Remains Serious 30

Minneapolis The truck drivers' strike here, which lasted for many days, has now come to an end after the labor union and employers signed an agreement. The agreement stipulates the rights that workers should enjoy after working in the factory for many years, prohibits differential treatment of workers who join the union, and establishes a basis for arbitration to resolve disputes. In addition, it also includes clauses regarding wages and working hours. It is generally believed that this result is a victory for the workers. It is estimated that one person died and about a hundred people were injured in this labor unrest. (Havas, 26th)

Toledo, Ohio Serious disturbances have been caused here by a strike at an electrical appliance factory. Demonstrators have clashed with the National Guard. A union leader has now declared that striking workers have rejected the conditions proposed by Labor Secretary Representative Taft at a meeting. Taft then declared to the union leader that the union leader should now propose conditions. Another shooting occurred at midnight last night, and a lieutenant officer of the National Guard and two bystanders were injured. Order was soon restored, but about 700 striking workers still surrounded the factory. (Havas, 26th)

(Washington) The continuing struggle between labor and capital has made people in the US capital uneasy. General Johnson, director of the Recovery Administration, and Labor Secretary Perkins have been warned that the spread of labor unrest is worrying. Riots have occurred in Toledo in the past two days. Today, the military and police used machine guns and tear gas to control everything, and local order was maintained. At the same time, the longshoremen's strike on the Pacific coast is also being actively mediated by those concerned, hoping to find a solution. (Reuter, 25th)

Turkey Orders Restrictions on Foreigners Practicing Professions: From Civil Servants to Chauffeurs, All Dismissed and Replaced by Turks 31

Istanbul Today, the government passed an order that foreigners employed in certain professions will be replaced by Turks. This order will affect thousands of foreigners living in Turkey. From May 21 to June 21, all foreigners serving as chauffeurs, barbers, tailors, shoemakers, hatters, translators, guides, stock exchange staff, and musicians must be dismissed. From June 21 to September 21, all foreign handicraft workers must stop working. From September 21 to November 21, foreigners employed in restaurants, cafes, etc., or street vendors, must be dismissed. From November 21 to January 21, 1935, foreign-run photography studios and printing houses must stop operating. From January 21, 1935 to March 21, foreigners selling state monopoly goods, artists, singers, and forwarding merchants must stop operating. From March 21 to May 21, managers of various businesses, government employees, and foreign staff in the Turkish government must be dismissed. This order was originally scheduled to be implemented last year, but was postponed due to protests from various governments. The most affected foreigners are Greeks, Italians, Persians, and British and Americans. These foreigners have lived here for decades, so their lives are particularly difficult to resolve. Some foreigners may change their nationality to Turkish, otherwise they may be expelled from the country. The Turkish government claims that there are many unemployed Turks, so it has to implement this measure, it is said. (Reuter, 25th)

Glimpse of the Attitudes of Britain and the United States at the Naval Conference: Naval Conference Said to Be Held in Paris; Britain Has New Strategy for Liaison with India 35

(New York) The People's Forum reported that some believe that Britain and the United States are about to hold talks on naval issues, intending to form a common front to deal with Japan's demand to increase its navy. However, official circles have indicated that there is no such meaning, saying that in the preliminary talks of the naval conference, naval issues will be considered from a technical point of view, without focusing on politics. In addition, the US government is currently building four 10,000-ton cruisers with 6-inch guns. When this plan was decided last winter, the British government advised Washington to postpone this construction plan, saying that naval issues would be renegotiated in the future. If the results show that it is appropriate to build these cruisers, the US government can start construction again. The US government did not listen to this advice, and Congress approved the government's expenditure to build three more 10,000-ton cruisers, which shows that there are differences of opinion between the two sides. However, although the US Navy has added new ships in this way, it has not exceeded the limitations set by the Washington Treaty. (Havas, 25th)

(London) The Japanese government has notified the British government that Japan is prepared to participate in the preliminary talks of the 1935 Naval Conference. British people familiar with this issue claim that the most wonderful thing about the 1935 Naval Conference would be to hold it in Paris, because it would be suitable for such a conference not to be held in countries that are more directly related. In addition, British strategy seems to be based on a new principle, namely, that if war breaks out, Britain's maritime liaison with India should use the Cape of Good Hope as a channel, rather than passing through the Suez Canal again. The British government believes that the eastern Mediterranean is vulnerable to air raids, so it has this new principle. It is estimated that the British government will give instructions to the British delegation participating in the naval talks based on this new principle and determine the attitude it should take. International Commercial Telegrams

Reuters Special Business Report Telegram, May 26th - Gold and Silver 74

▲ London Gold Price: The London gold price today is 136 shillings and 6 pence, down half a penny from yesterday.

▲ London Silver: The London silver market saw limited trading this morning, with US buying and Indian selling. The spot price is 19 and a half pence, and the futures price is 19.5625 pence, both down 0.0625 pence from yesterday.

▲ New York Silver: The New York silver market opened quietly, with mixed sentiment. The authorities are insisting on the tax clause in the silver legislation bill, so speculators have little interest in the silver market. The price is similar to London. The forward opening price is 10 to 16 points lower than yesterday's closing price.

▲ Bombay Silver: The Bombay silver market closed quietly today, with both spot and futures prices falling. The spot price is 53 rupees and 11 annas.

▲ Special Telegram: Jardine Matheson received a telegram from London on the 26th, stating that the London Financial Times' New York dispatch reported that the US House of Representatives committee has heard opinions from all sides regarding the silver legislation bill. Financial experts believe that the London silver market is very influential and can control the silver price. If the bill passes, the world silver price will exceed 50 US cents per ounce. It is estimated that the US domestic silver reserves are between 150 million and 250 million ounces.

Exchange Rates 75

▲ Anglo-American: The London foreign exchange market was very quiet this morning. The opening exchange rate for Anglo-American was 5.055 yuan, the same as yesterday's closing exchange rate for American-British. The price was slightly weaker before noon, and the closing price was 5.090625 yuan, down 4375 from the opening price. One US dollar equals 3 shillings and 11.45 pence.

▲ Anglo-French: The opening price was 77.09 francs, down three points from yesterday's closing price. It rose slightly later, but fell back slightly at closing, remaining at 77.09 francs, the same as the opening price.

▲ American-British: The opening exchange rate was 5.09125 yuan, down 375 from yesterday's closing price. It fell slightly later, with the latest price being 5.08875 yuan, down 15 from the opening price.

▲ American-French: The opening exchange rate was 6.6025, down one-half from yesterday's closing price.

Cotton and Wheat 76

▲ American Cotton: The cotton market opened with mixed sentiment and sluggish conditions. Buying by traders and the Far East, as well as short covering by retail investors towards the end of the week, absorbed the liquidation of July positions and selling by locals and the South. Later, due to retail buying and a lack of pressure from sellers, the price rose slightly, and the market stabilized.

▲ British Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market is closed today.

▲ Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market initially fell due to profit-taking but rebounded slightly due to Japanese buying. At 5:30 PM, the July-August price for White Lorchi cotton was 196 rupees, up four annas from yesterday.

Japanese Soldiers Mutiny at Shenyang Station; Oppose Transfer to Northern Manchuria; Japanese Claim Soldiers Have Been "Reddened" 104

Japanese-Puppet Opium Policy: Establishing the Daman Company; Capital of One Million Yuan; Poisoning the People of Four Provinces 105

Changchun Correspondence: It is an undeniable fact that Japan intends to use opium to exterminate our race. According to investigations, among the thirty million compatriots in the Northeast, as many as nine million are addicted to opium. They still consider this insufficient. Recently, in view of the opium purchases in Rehe Province and western Xing'an Province, although they are conducted by purchasers designated by the Rehe Opium Monopoly Bureau through its various sub-bureaus, the current purchasing situation in various places has become a competitive trend due to the scattered organization of the purchasers and a lack of control. This has made purchasing difficult and impossible to implement, resulting in smuggling. The Japanese-puppet authorities' response to this matter has been decided to adopt the organization of the puppet capital's Monopoly Bureau, under the guidance of Japanese Takeuchi, director of the Chengde Opium Monopoly Bureau. It intends to unite opium merchants from various places to organize the Daman Company, specializing in purchasing opium produced within the jurisdiction of the Rehe Monopoly Bureau, so that all opium produced will be transferred to the Monopoly Bureau. Zhang Yu Xuan is to be the general manager of the company, and Hu Mo Jie is to be the deputy manager. In addition, powerful opium merchants from Chengde, Pingquan, Baliwei, Lingyuan, Chaoyang, Chifeng, Weichang, and other places are all members. The purchase is funded by the buyers with a capital of one million yuan in puppet currency. It was founded on April 1st and received a permission order from the Puppet Ministry of Finance on April 20th. The company plans to purchase ten million yuan worth of opium in Rehe Province and western Xing'an Province. The opium is charged a handling fee of about one-tenth of a yuan per tael by the Monopoly Bureau. Since its founding, it has purchased about 300,000 taels of opium. The company's activities and locations of established branches are listed in detail below: (1) Location of branches and distribution of funds: Chengde 40,000, Pingquan 200,000, Lingyuan 70,000, Chaoyang 200,000, Chifeng 300,000, Weichang 200,000; (2) Sub-branches: 5 in Chengde jurisdiction, 2 in Pingquan jurisdiction, 4 in Chifeng jurisdiction, 1 in Weichang jurisdiction, 3 in Lingyuan jurisdiction, 5 in Chaoyang jurisdiction, and planned to open sub-branches in Fengning Anjiangtun and Tiantu towns; (3) Anti-Smuggling Measures: Currently, 15 secret investigation groups have been dispatched to the customs borders and provincial borders, and they are currently investigating.

Details of Rehe Volunteers Sacrificing Themselves Resisting Japan; Volunteer Liu Liangshan Killed 400 Japanese Soldiers; Exhausted of Ammunition and Without Reinforcements, Surrounded by the Enemy, He Committed Suicide 106

The area around Wujiazi, Sanjiazi, and Weijiagou, the largest base of the Rehe Volunteer Army for the past two years, has suffered a brutal siege, burning, and killing by the Japanese army. According to recent reports from Rehe, Liu Cunqi, also known as Liangshan, the commander of the 9th Division of the Rehe National Salvation Army, was the bravest of the Rehe volunteers. He previously fought against several thousand Japanese soldiers in Wujiazi Weijiagou. In that battle, over a thousand volunteers and civilians died. At that time, Liu, wielding two guns, broke through the encirclement and escaped into the eastern mountain mine tunnels of Weijiagou. The Japanese army, because there were many tunnels, sent two soldiers to guard each tunnel. They retreated after ten days. Afterwards, the people entered the tunnel and saw that Liu had committed suicide. Only one bullet remained in his handgun. Everyone who saw this wept bitterly. Since the events in the East, many patriotic men in the Northeast have risen up to resist Japan. There are few who can lead by example, not avoiding sacrifice, like Liu. As for being exhausted of ammunition and without reinforcements, being surrounded by the enemy, and still committing suicide to show his steadfast will, he can truly be said to have done his utmost. No wonder those who saw this wept as if their hearts would break. According to reports, Liu was initially a sheep butcher. He enlisted in the army at the age of twenty. No one in the Liaoxi area does not know the name of Liangshan. Liu had a shiny bald head, so he called himself Liangshan. In mid-January of the previous year, he led patriotic youths from the Northeast to organize a volunteer army and recaptured Jinxi County. In just over twenty days, he killed three to four hundred Japanese soldiers. Japanese newspapers reported that the Battle of Jinxi was one of the battles with the most Japanese casualties since the Battle of Jiangqiao in Ma Zhanshan. The Liaoxi Volunteer Army Heng Qiao called himself Liu's unit. The Japanese army was shocked by his bravery and dared not advance. Liu initially served as the commander of the 36th Route Army of the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army and later served as the commander of the 9th Division of the Northeast National Salvation Army. The army attacked Yi on October 20th of the previous year and Jin on the 25th. Liu was in charge of the main force on both occasions. He had accumulated over one hundred acres of fields. He has an old wife and an eldest son of about twenty-two years old, who is married and has a grandson, who is adorable. His second son is over ten years old. Currently, they are all unknown where they are drifting. (Northeast News Agency)

Post-Fourth Army Work in Longgang: Officers Supervise Road Construction, Soldiers Cultivate Land for the People 107

Nanchang Dispatch: Since the start of the Fifth Encirclement Campaign, the speed of the Northern Route Army's advance has truly set a new record in bandit suppression. After the Sixth Route Army recaptured Shanggu and Longgang, it immediately began building blockhouses and roads. The 59th and 90th Divisions of the Fourth Army put forth the most effort. The army officers inspected the work daily, and although the materials used were local, they did not harm the people at all. The roadbeds were solid, the surfaces smooth, the edges planted with trees, all in good order. Pavilions and public restrooms were also constructed in a very rational manner, making it a model highway in Jiangxi. Furthermore, many villages and houses in the Shanggu and Quejiaping areas were burned down by the Red bandits, and the residents were forced to move elsewhere, unable to return, thus delaying spring plowing. When the 90th Division was stationed there, it used local bamboo, wood, and thatch to build barracks, stretching for ten *li*, the lights at night as bright as a city scene, showing no sign of desolation. The officers and soldiers of the division rested there, climbing mountains and peaks several times a day, training diligently, showing a vigorous spirit, and fully displaying the vitality of modern soldiers. The nearby fields, because many people had not returned, were about to become barren. Division Commander Ou Zhen and Chief of Staff Huang Zhanchun, believing that spring plowing could not be abandoned, specially ordered their troops to cultivate the land for the people, personally leading the officers and soldiers to plant rice seedlings in the fields, setting an example for all units. Senior officials, after commanding troops, personally cultivated the land, filled with enthusiasm, plowing and harrowing like old farmers. The officers and soldiers worked harmoniously and diligently, planting dozens of *mu* of rice fields in two days. The people were all grateful and spread the word, happily returning one after another. It is also heard that orders have been issued to all regimental officers and soldiers to allocate labor to cultivate the land for the people, so that the residents can return to harvest. It is found that the bandit areas have been ravaged by bandits for many years, and now they have seen the light of day again. The Fourth Army has always been known for its bravery and good fighting, and strict discipline. Now they can also get close to the people, and the people deeply love them. The people's support is enough to affect the success or failure of the encirclement campaign. Seeing this, the pacification of the Red bandits is not far off.

Anhui Construction Department's Emergency Relief for Rural Economy: Organizing a Design Committee 108

Anqing Dispatch: In Anhui Province, frequent floods and bandit disasters have occurred in recent years, leading to stagnant sales of agricultural products and a decline in the rural economy, with the urban economy also trending towards collapse. In order to seek emergency relief, the Construction Department has specially organized an Emergency Relief for Rural Design Committee. Its design scope includes: (1) Promoting the planting and expanding the improvement of agricultural products; (2) Promoting the improvement of agricultural product manufacturing; (3) Removing obstacles to the transportation and sale of agricultural products; (4) Seeking convenience in the transportation and sale of agricultural products; (5) Regulating and managing special agricultural products; (6) Liaising and communicating with the sales areas of agricultural products in this province; (7) Promoting rural cooperation and regulating rural finance. The department has already dispatched Secretary Chen Yan, Wang Shoujiong, Xia Gengying, Section Chief Yuan Fen, Technical Officer Fang Junqiang, Technicians Duan Tianjue and Hong Changyi as members of the committee, and designated Chen Yan, Yuan Fen, and Fang Junqiang as standing committee members. Preparations are now actively underway, and it will be established soon (24th).

Dredging Project of Jiangbei's Six-Pond River to be Completed by the End of the Month 109

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The Jiangbei Six-Pond River is crucial for transportation, irrigation, and drinking water for Huaiyin, Suqian, Siyang, Shuyang, Lianshui, Donghai, and Guanyun counties. Since construction began on January 1st of this year, the project has progressed exceptionally quickly. The project within Huaiyin and Siyang counties has been completed, and the remaining counties are expected to be completed in the near future. The construction process of the river and its recent situation are roughly as follows:

This dredging project of the Six-Pond River is being carried out entirely according to the three principles decided at the Jiangsu Province Six-Pond River Dredging Conference last year: (1) Deepen the riverbed from Xinei to Longgou to facilitate drainage; (2) Widen the dikes from Guji to Longgou to increase capacity; (3) Repair all dikes to prevent flooding. It is estimated that 2 million cubic meters of earth will be dredged and 3.5 million cubic meters of earth will be used to repair the dikes. The cost of earthwork, food, and the number of workers recruited from each county were also decided at the conference. The minimum price for dike construction is 4 *fen* per cubic meter, the maximum is 6 *fen*, and the average is 5 *fen*, which is determined temporarily by the engineering office based on local conditions and distance. The cost of excavating river soil is 7.7 *fen* per cubic meter for dirt, and 1 *jiao* per cubic meter for sand and gravel, averaging 8.5 *fen* per cubic meter, for a total cost of over 600,000 yuan. The number of workers recruited is estimated to be 8,000 in Suqian, 6,000 in Siyang, 4,000 in Huaiyin, 14,000 in Shuyang, 10,000 in Lianshui, 6,000 in Donghai, and 12,000 in Guanyun. After the conference closed on November 30th, the provincial government appointed Xu Dingkang, director of the Jiangbei Canal Engineering Bureau, to concurrently serve as the director of the Six-Pond River Dredging Project Office. Xu departed from Yang for Qing on December 9th and established the engineering office on the 10th, dividing the entire river project into five sections, each with an engineer. After that, they began surveying the river channel, and the survey was completed by the end of the year. Dredging began on January 1st of this year, but the work was not rapid due to the Lunar New Year. Later, after the engineering office repeatedly ordered the counties to work hard, it began to proceed actively. The project within Huaiyin was completed on April 10th, and Siyang was completed on April 20th. The rest have also completed seven or eight tenths, and it should be fully completed by the end of May (26th).

Suzhou: Religious Philosophy Research Society Spreads Superstition 110

Recently, a so-called Religious Philosophy Research Society was established in the Northern Temple on Pingmen Road, causing a social craze, with the whole city going mad. The details of the situation and an analysis of its content are as follows:

The society has an Ancestral Hall, in which hangs a portrait of a Mr. Xiao, neither Confucian nor Buddhist, with his hair tied up and holding a cleansing vase. In front of the portrait is a table, on which incense is burned. In front of the table are more than twenty *futons*. In addition, there is another Light Hall, in which a yellow cloth is hung like a silver screen. In front is an offering table, on which incense, flowers, and fresh fruit are offered. Two rows of *futons* are also arranged in front of the table. All who enter must take off their hats and shoes, hold their breath, and enter, performing the Three Kneelings and Nine Kowtows. Moreover, not just anyone can enter; they must be someone with some reputation in society and recognized as having innate goodness, before they can be led in by someone from the society. It is said that after performing the ceremony and gazing at the screen, one can see the forms of all the Buddhas and Bodhisattvas as one wishes. In the end, it is just a kind of legend. All those from various circles who join, regardless of gender, can do so with a member's introduction and paying a fee as usual. The procedure is to first pay respects to the statue of the founder, kneeling on a *futon* for about two hours, called "receiving light," and then enter the Light Hall to worship as usual. In this way, they have the supernatural power to treat people's illnesses. The society claims to be a mixture of Confucianism, Buddhism, and Taoism, separately worshipping Mr. Xiao as the founder and establishing a new school, taking not feeling the pulse and not using medicine to treat people's illnesses as its work. After joining the society, one must sacrifice everything and dedicate oneself to the society, including women. The reason is that so-called "adult gentlemen" have also joined to call upon each other, so many people believe in it. The gods worshipped by the people in the society, some of whom may never see the teacher, Mr. Xiao, in their lifetime, suddenly arrived the other day, gave a public lecture, and hosted a vegetarian meal. However, Mr. Xiao's way of treating diseases is to use the righteousness of silently reciting the twenty characters of loyalty, forgiveness, integrity, and clarity, which is different from his disciples' claim that "the Bodhisattva will save you." According to some people, Mr. Xiao is like the so-called "senior brother" of the Boxer Rebellion. Since the establishment of the society, in less than two weeks, no fewer than thousands of patients from far and near have come to seek treatment every day. Currently, party members Jiang Yuqi and Zhu Mengmei have submitted a report to the county party headquarters, stating that the society has not yet been ordered by the party headquarters to be approved for preparation, and has already been giving diagnosis for treating people's illnesses without medicine or feeling the pulse, causing foolish men and women to flock to it like crazy. No fewer than one or two thousand people go to seek treatment every day. The method of treating diseases is to take a piece of gauze, which is written with a talisman by the practitioner, burned to ashes, and given to the patient to take, saying that it can cure the disease. In the end, no one who has been treated has seen any effect, and it is said that there is even a risk of worsening the condition. This is blatant promotion of superstition, confusing the foolish people, disrupting social views, and endangering lives. It is requested that the county government be transferred to strictly order the Public Security Bureau to dissolve it immediately. The county party headquarters' Standing Committee member Zhu, based on the report, has sent a letter to the county government to investigate and handle it.

Xuzhuang Sailing Ship Encountered Bandits En Route 111

A sailing ship traveling between Suzhou and Xuzhuang, owned by Ge Huangyao, encountered a bandit ship near Shangfang Mountain in Shihu on the afternoon of the 25th. There were four bandits with guns who boarded the ship and robbed the passengers. All six passengers were searched, and more than one hundred yuan were robbed. Afterwards, the shipowner reported the theft to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Wuxi: Implementing Silkworm Cocoon Control: Officials and Merchants Firmly Contend 112

Since the Construction Department of this county promulgated the Cocoon Control Measures, various parties have had different opinions. Therefore, at 2:00 p.m. on the 24th, an emergency meeting was held at the Silk Factory Trade Association, and four measures were decided and submitted to the authorities for a petition to postpone implementation. The situation was reported in this newspaper, stating that when funds are needed for unregistered cocoon businesses, they should all be rejected, etc. The contention between officials and merchants is quite firm. Yan Shenyu, the magistrate of this county, and Cai Jingde, the deputy director of the model district, considering that the cocoon market is approaching and it is difficult to delay, specially went to the province the other day to ask Shen, the director of the Construction Department, for instructions on a solution. Director Shen, after hearing the report, was quite firm, stating that cocoon control is one of the entire provincial measures to rescue the silk industry. The Chinese silk industry has reached its most dangerous state. If improvements are not sought urgently, it will inevitably be subject to international competition and fall into bankruptcy. The livelihoods of farmers and the status of merchants will be fundamentally affected. In any case, there can be no changes. As for the collection of improvement fees, Zhejiang Province has already implemented it last autumn and is collecting it slightly again this year. There is precedent. Moreover, the improvement fees are specifically for the improvement of the silk industry and are different from taxes. If there are a few people who do not understand the situation, disregard the future interests of farmers, and intentionally obstruct the progress of the business, they will be severely suppressed. Those who do not comply with the measures to register and accept customers to start a business will have their cocoon licenses revoked. If they do not register or pay the guarantee money and collect cocoons without authorization, once discovered, in addition to detaining the dry cocoons, they will also be charged double the improvement fee as punishment. After receiving the instructions, Yan and Cai returned to Wuxi yesterday morning (26th) and decided to handle the matter in accordance with Director Shen's instructions. Therefore, it is feared that a solution cannot be reached for a while.

Rice and Bean Industry Changes to New Measuring Instruments 113

The case of promoting the new system of weights and measures in this county has been implemented by various industries one after another. Only the rice and bean industry has been slow to implement it. After repeated urging by officials, the Rice and Bean Industry Association has successively sent the measuring instruments used to the county for inspection. More than 340 pieces have already been sent, and the county government will complete the inspection of the qualified measuring units, which can then be standardized.

Silk and Iron Tycoon Goes Bankrupt for Millions 114

Zhou Zhaofu, a resident of Dongfeng, Zhouxin Town in this county, is a tycoon in the silk and iron industry, owning assets of four to five million. His business operations extend to various ports in Shanghai, Wuhan, Suzhou, Wuxi, and Dalian. His father, Shunqing, was a fourth-rank official in the late Qing Dynasty and had jointly founded the Xincheng Bank with Prince Qing Yikuang, causing a sensation. After Shunqing's death, Zhaofu followed in his father's footsteps and continued the business established by his father. In addition to the Yuchang, Shenchang, and Dingchang three silk factories in Wuxi, there are also the Xinyuanlai Smelting Workshop in the Nanshi area of Shanghai (jointly operated with the Hu family, with assets of 400,000), the Yixu Wharf in the Nanshi area of Shanghai (with assets of over 100,000), the Xinzhenyuan Smelting Workshop in Suzhou, the Suzhou Yuchangxiang Iron Company (with assets of 100,000), the Shanghai Zhengchang Iron Company, as well as the Pudong warehouse, the Zhengchangren Iron Company in Hankou, the Shengyuan Oil Mill in Dalian (jointly operated with Ye Hongying), etc. He also owns land worth over 20,000 yuan in Nagasaki, Japan. He owns a residence on Qipu Road in Shanghai, more than 3,000 *mu* of farmland and street houses in the northern township of Wuxi and Zhouxin Town. In recent years, Zhou's business has failed, causing the Shanghai Zhengchang Iron Company, the Hankou Zhengchangren Iron Company, etc. to close down one after another. The residence on Qipu Road in Shanghai and the Pudong warehouse have also been mortgaged. Recently, due to financial difficulties, he has declared bankruptcy, owing more than 1.5 million yuan. He has entrusted lawyer Sun Zuhong to liquidate. For the debts owed to banks and money shops, the Yuchang, Dingchang, and Shenchang three silk factories have been mortgaged, but this is still not enough. For the debts owed to depositors, totaling more than 200,000, it is proposed to compensate with more than 680 *mu* of farmland, with each 1,000 yuan receiving about 1.3 *mu* of land. The creditors do not agree, resulting in no result. A creditor group has now been formed to negotiate. However, it is heard that Zhou Zhaofu still has 400,000 yuan in deposits at the Bank of China and more than 2,000 *mu* of farmland, which are said to have been donated to the Yizhuang.

Jiangyin: Salted Yellow Croaker Refuses to Collect Business Tax 115

Wu Xiaochi, director of the Jiangjing Business Tax Bureau, sent a letter to the Fish and North Goods Trade Association, requesting them to collect business tax on salted yellow croaker, as the yellow croaker season is approaching. The association sent a letter to the Hupu Fish Trade Association in Changshu for consultation. It was reported that fish tax and fishery tax had long been explicitly exempted by the National Government. Salted yellow croaker is collected from the ocean by fishing boats and is not transported for sale, so it is different from the nature of business. Moreover, *lijin* has also been abolished long ago, and collecting tax on goods is a disguised form of restoring *lijin*. The business tax should naturally be refused.

Jiading: Butcher Gu Jixiang Kills His Father 116

Gu Fengxiang, aged 65, of Gujiazhai, Zouma Township in the Second District, had a son, A Xiang, who worked as a butcher. On the morning of the 25th, father and son went to Chenjiahang Town to buy wine and drank together. A Xiang drank wildly and became drunk. After drinking, they went home together. Fengxiang ordered his family to dry salted fish. A Xiang objected, and they disagreed. A Xiang went to his room and took out the sharp knife he used for butchering pigs and stabbed his father in the upper part of his thigh, piercing through his lower abdomen. Fengxiang immediately fainted and died shortly after. The local township police officer Meng Zhendu reported the incident to the Nanxiang Public Security Bureau, which dispatched patrol chief Sun Yuzhen and police officers to investigate and confirm the facts. However, the murder weapon was missing. A Xiang was taken to the bureau and sent to the County Public Security Bureau. Director Xue Bingyang interrogated him, and he confessed that he was 46 years old and that he had stabbed his father. He said that he stabbed him in the thigh because he was drunk at about 9:00 a.m. The county government detained him that evening. The next morning, presiding judge Shao Ling and police officers went to the countryside to conduct an on-site investigation and confirmed that he had been stabbed to death before his death. The family was ordered to prepare the coffin.

Qingjiang: New County Magistrate Takes Office 117

Lu Cangeng, the former magistrate of Huaiyin County, was dismissed by the provincial government for his weak efforts in recruiting labor to dredge the Six-Pond River. Qi Yunlong, a counselor of the National Government, was appointed to replace him. Qi arrived in Pu on the afternoon of the 23rd and took office yesterday morning (24th). After taking office, in addition to gathering all the large and small officials retained in the government to give a speech in the Zhongshan Hall, he also went to the Commissioner's Office and the Gao Fa Branch Court to inquire about the political and judicial directions of the county. He had long talks with Secretary Zhang, Chief of Staff Wu, President Sheng, and Chief Xu of the branch court. He returned to the county government at noon.

Speech by the Head of the Delegation 127

Zhan Jing Tang, the head of the Qingdao Industrial Inspection Delegation, reported, "Our delegation's mission in coming to Shanghai to inspect industry is twofold: Firstly, Shanghai and Qingdao are the two major ports of China. Geographically, there are close relations in commerce and trade. The value of imported goods through Qingdao's Jiaohai Customs approximates over 50 million yuan in national currency annually. Given the importance of this port, it is imperative that entrepreneurs, traders, and economists pay special attention and jointly seek ways to recover our rights and interests. Secondly, Qingdao has only been under our control for a little over ten years. During this time, it has experienced multiple civil wars, leading to extreme panic in the market. Since Mayor Shen took office, he has vigorously promoted industry and developed the market. In recent years, there has been a slight industrial foundation, but compared with the construction technology achievements of major factories in Shanghai, the difference is like night and day. We hope that entrepreneurs and technicians in Shanghai will provide more assistance and contributions. Thirdly, Qingdao has such a good port, and the annual consumption is so large. The raw materials of inland industrial products are abundant, such as coal, tobacco, peanuts, cowhide, and wool, which can be fully supplied. For every bit more that domestic goods are sold, a portion of economic rights and interests is recovered. We hope that the gentlemen of the press will vigorously promote and advocate on behalf of the 400,000 compatriots in Qingdao, to treat Qingdao as the Qingdao of all Chinese people, and to build Qingdao into a Chicago of the United States or a Manchester of the United Kingdom, instead of viewing Qingdao as an oriental Switzerland or a playground park within our country. Moreover, our delegation believes that the press represents public opinion, and our industrial circles regard the gentlemen of the press as our nurses. Qingdao's industry is still in its infancy, and Shanghai's newspapers are popular throughout the country and overseas. One call from the top will resonate across all the mountains. Therefore, Qingdao's new industries, such as needle making, frozen powder manufacturing, cowhide glue manufacturing, and China Stone Company, all rely on sales channels to have hope for development. The Shanghai press is the mentor of Qingdao's nascent industry, which is also the heartfelt prayer of our delegation."

Mr. Ma Yinliang, representing the press, stood up to reply, saying, "We are deeply honored by your delegation's invitation. Many people from various places come to Shanghai for sightseeing, but none leave a deeper impression on us than your delegation. Secondly, your delegation takes industrial inspection as its mission, breaking away from the regionalism of the past, which will undoubtedly be beneficial to the development of our country's industrial future. Now that we are about to part, I would like to offer a cup of wine on behalf of the hosts, to wish your delegation good health and the development of Qingdao's industry."
