Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Ramblings

What Kind of Elections Do We Need? 287

— Li Qiu

In recent weeks, Mr. Gongpu has repeatedly raised the issue of improving elections in this publication. Naturally, this issue is not only of great significance in promoting municipal or local autonomy and other practical situations, but also a vital problem to be solved in the overall political transformation of China.

Although many elections in China's past have failed under unsound conditions, this can never be said to be the fault of "elections" themselves. Because elections are just a method. Whenever people want to place the final right of judgment on social affairs in the hands of the majority, there is fundamentally no other way than the method of elections.

Therefore, what we are now demanding for local autonomy and improved elections is, in fact, to save the development of the spirit of democracy. We believe this is the minimum effort to save the national crisis through political transformation.

Therefore, the question now is not whether we need to improve elections, but mainly what kind of elections we need. Regarding this, I believe:

First, what we need is universal suffrage. The gradual expansion of suffrage in modern times has allowed past class elections to progress to universal elections. Therefore, we demand the abolition of all restrictions based on religion, economy, social status, and gender. Except for underage children, patients with mental illness, and those deprived of their civil rights, everyone should have the obligation and right to participate in elections.

Second, we demand the expansion of the real power of elections. The value of suffrage is mainly reflected in the number of elected officials. The participation of the people in elections is not only to elect advisory bodies for the government, but, more importantly, to elect people who can represent their opinions and directly participate in the thorough resolution and implementation of all major national or local issues. Therefore, we demand that the real power of elections should be expanded. At the same time, we also want to save the implementation of the rights of initiative, referendum, and recall, because these three are interrelated.

Third, attention to election methods. We know that the value and effectiveness of suffrage are greatly related to voting methods. Open elections cannot fully express the will of the voters, and the "designated" election method completely loses the meaning of elections. Now, the election systems of various countries have almost all been changed to secret ballot systems. Therefore, we also demand that this election method be practically used in all elections in China.

Fourth, mandatory elections should be implemented. Suffrage is not only a right of the people, but also an obligation. Election is a public duty, and the state must use all means to ensure that the people fulfill this duty. In the past, most people in our country were often indifferent to elections, on the one hand being manipulated by local bullies and ambitious politicians, and on the other hand causing the people to have no interest in politics. Therefore, we advocate that the government should follow the example of countries such as Belgium, the Netherlands, Czechoslovakia, and Spain, and implement a mandatory election system, stipulating that those who do not participate in elections should be subject to certain economic or reputational penalties.

Fifth, demand strict laws against election fraud. Election fraud was a common phenomenon in our country in the past. Now, if we don't talk about elections, then so be it. But when we do talk about elections, on the positive side, we demand to improve the political level of the general public. On the negative side, we demand a strict law against election fraud. The state must use laws to stipulate that anyone who bribes, entertains, intimidates, impersonates, or illegally uses election funds or election campaigners must be given strict punishment.

The above points are our minimum requirements for improving elections. Some people say that this is just an unattainable high-sounding argument. In fact, we know that if an election can truly represent public opinion, and if the result of an election can be supported by the majority of the people, then apart from an election based on the above points, what better method do we have? Therefore, we hope that the authorities in charge of elections should take this as a goal to promote the implementation of sound elections. Whether it is central politics, local autonomy, or social organizations, if there cannot be perfect and sound elections, then all ideals cannot be achieved.

Indeed, "having elections is better than not having elections," but simply "having elections" is not enough. We still need to demand more perfect elections within "having elections"!

Life

Blood Rice 288

— Long Lai

Living in this unreasonable society where "the rich's wine and meat rot, and there are frozen bones on the road," ordinary people who cannot smell wine and meat, struggling on the line of cold rice and death, in order to live, some have to reluctantly auction off their labor at a low price, and some even sell their own children cheaply, and insist on exchanging the blood of their bodies for leftovers to fill their stomachs. This is what I want to talk about here: the hardworking women who are hired by noble people to be wet nurses.

Just go to the "Employment Agency" in Beiping, the "Job Introduction Shop" in Shanghai, or the "Human Market" in Chengdu, and the "Guild Hall" in Chongqing. We will see these "blood sellers" squatting or sitting in rows like exhibits, waiting to be sold. Their eyes, filled with the bitter tears of leaving their husbands and children, are hungrily and concernedly fixed on passers-by. When they finally wait for a customer to come in, they fearfully and anxiously hold out a pair of eggplant-like breasts, allowing people to choose the fat and pick the lean, examine and fondle them. As a result, the one who is sold is both sad and happy and goes with the master (mostly to be subjected to a blood test by the doctor). The ones who are left behind after being picked and chosen are dejectedly waiting for customers again. Who can see all this without feeling that it is a tragic tragedy? Aren't "blood sellers" even more pitiful than ordinary laborers?

Naturally, to give their blood to the sons and daughters of the nobles to suck, they must first put their own children aside: the better thing is to spend some money to entrust them to someone else's house, or leave them at home to feed them rice soup. Otherwise, if there is no one to entrust or no one to take care of them, they have to endure the pain and simply give them to others or abandon them on the roadside or in the alley. When a woman who works as a wet nurse in this way holds someone else's child to feed her own milk, how deeply she must feel the pain in her heart! Especially when she sees someone else's child opening his little mouth and smiling at her, stretching out his little hands and waving to her so adorably.

In terms of responsibility and work, wet nurses and ordinary maids and sisters seem to have no difference on the surface, but in reality, they are much more arduous than maids and sisters. They not only bear the responsibility of feeding the child, but also have to bear the heavy responsibility of the child's development, health, illness, hygiene, etc. Therefore, once they are hired, they completely lose their freedom in terms of body and action. I remember there was such a tragicomedy: in a mansion where a couple both claimed to be educators, the hostess supervised the wet nurse every day to rub some cold cream and powder on her old melon-peel-like face, saying that her face was too ugly, and the girl would be afraid of resembling her in the future if she drank her milk. As a result, her face, which had been roughened by the wind and frost and haggard by labor, became feverish and painful from being pickled by cold cream and powder. In the end, she couldn't laugh or cry when she looked in the mirror. Speaking of action, it is simply no different from a prisoner in jail, because the young master or lady cannot go without milk for half a day or a night, so they never get to go home for a year or so. They are clearly married women, but the master insists that they keep "live widowhood." Not only that, but even walking casually on the street or in the neighbor's house is subject to interference. If the child accidentally catches a cold and sneezes, then the master will scold her even more for catching a cold because she took the child out for a walk. The more severe masters even use "deducting wages" and "getting out" to suppress her.

Changing the child's clothes and diapers, playing with the child, feeding the child, and rocking the cradle day and night are the general tasks of being a wet nurse. In addition, buying vegetables, cooking,

Page 20

and sewing are also things that must be done. If the child is a little older, gradually grows teeth, and the sleeping time decreases, and can barely crawl, then the wet nurse's work is not easy. She has to be careful at all times to prevent him from falling, and she cannot leave her post even when sleeping. At this time, the child's every move is not as regular as when he was first born. Take his feeding, for example, before he grows his little teeth, he will tightly bite the breast and rub his gums while feeding. After the teeth come out, he will use his melon-seed-sized new teeth to tear and bite the nipple, often causing the wet nurse's face to twitch, but she cannot complain. She has to swallow the sour tears silently into her stomach. Man eats man, it's true!

When the child is eight or nine months old, his appetite also increases compared to before. The wet nurse always humbly fears that her milk cannot satisfy him, and at the same time, she has to be attentive to the master to show that her milk is good—fearing that her rice bowl will be in trouble. Therefore, whether it is day or night, as long as the child cries, she immediately puts the breast into his mouth, letting the blood-sucking baby slowly suck, even if sometimes sucking hurts her flesh and swallows her blood, she has to endure the pain.

The leftovers in the messy cups and plates are the only food the master gives to the wet nurse. The clothes they wear are the moldy old clothes and pants from the bottom of their chests. As for their wages, the highest is no more than ten dollars, and six or eight dollars is the most popular price. If their own children are still being raised by others, then, apart from the cost of raising their own children, what they earn from the cold rice and leftovers is just a body of anemic thin bones. This is the price of "blood sellers," this is the life of those who eat blood rice.

Chinese Teacher 289

— Wen Yu

People all know that Chinese teachers are the most hardworking kind of teachers, but what exactly is the picture of toil unfolding in their lives is something that people may not fully understand. In the past year, I had the honor of being such a teacher in a private middle school in this city. I can't say that I really have much experience, but I don't deny that I do have some observations.

First of all, what I need to bring up is the incorrect concept that society has of these teachers. They think that education is noble, and therefore think that teachers, especially Chinese teachers, are eminent scholars and recluses who have not been stained with any earthly concerns. But the truth is absolutely the opposite. They are not only not any eminent scholars and recluses, they not only need bread like ordinary people, but they have to wage a fierce struggle for survival for bread. In this era of talent surplus?), in order to hold on to their jobs, they have to use all kinds of methods to guard against competitors. Even if they want to be noble, they cannot.

Now I will show here the dark side of their lives. Disregarding their health and ability, they often teach at two, three, or even four or more schools. Some teach as many as five or six classes. In terms of clock hours, some teach thirty-six hours per week. They are completely using their bodies like machines. There is almost no talk of teaching efficiency here; we only see a group of people trying to get by struggling and wriggling.

The reason for this is obviously the excessive meager treatment, coupled with arrears of salary, so that their monthly hard-earned income is still sometimes unable to support their families. In this situation, what good way is there to call them to pay attention to teaching efficiency and take on fewer clock hours?

According to the general situation of the educational circles in China today, their hard work is valued by the hour, depending on the nature of public and private schools and the degree of development of that school, and not only the amount of remuneration. Currently, there is such a situation in Shanghai: in a middle school with only one or two years of history and about 100 students, it is very difficult for teachers to receive their salary, although the letter of appointment may stipulate that they should be able to receive five cents per hour. They are not necessarily completely "fulfilling their obligations," because the school still solves their living problems such as "food" and "accommodation." At least there is the benefit of "being able to live in a hotel without paying," which can be said to be of a "semi-obligatory" nature. Sometimes, unexpectedly, they may even be able to receive five to ten yuan per month in "travel expenses."

In a slightly larger private middle school, Chinese teachers can reliably get five cents an hour for their "tuition fee." If you teach Chinese in a certain grade for six hours a week in such a school, then you can get twelve yuan, which is considered a "cigarette money."

In a more "established" private middle school, Chinese teachers can get seven to eight cents per hour. There is one school I know of that is like this: Junior high school one, seven cents per hour, junior high school two, seven and a half cents, junior high school three, eight cents. (Most of what is said in this article refers to the situation of junior high schools.) Private middle schools with one dollar an hour are extremely rare in Shanghai. Public junior high schools can generally reach this amount. In short, this is completely different from the situation in some provinces outside of Shanghai, where junior high school Chinese teachers can receive one yuan, one yuan and twenty-five cents, or one yuan and a half per hour.

Although the treatment is so low, they are required to work twice as hard. Chinese teachers need more time to correct Chinese papers than to teach classes. There is not a single Chinese teacher who does not have a headache looking at some half-baked papers. Normally, a Chinese teacher who is not very experienced can only correct three or four papers in an hour, and those who are more efficient can only correct six or seven papers. However, there are many "lazy" methods in between, which is to judge at a glance—narrative essays are easy to correct, argumentative essays are the most difficult. The best thing is to have the students write something similar (or even the same), for example, you ask them to write according to the "outline" you give, or ask them to translate a classical Chinese text into vernacular Chinese, or write a "sketch" of more than 100 words, etc. The easiest thing to do is to tell them a short story and ask them to write it down, or to present a short text from the textbook and ask them to delete the sentences that can be omitted to shorten the text. Correcting twelve or thirteen or even fifteen or sixteen papers like this only takes you an hour. I remember that once at a banquet held by the Beixin Bookstore to promote its "Mixed Mandarin" and "Beixin Anthology" to Chinese teachers in middle schools in this city, a very healthy teacher said that he could correct fifteen or sixteen papers in an hour. I guessed that he might be using this time-saving method!

Some people may criticize this kind of teacher for being irresponsible, but they really have no choice. They are not only too busy, but also too tired. Normally, a Chinese teacher teaching 20 hours a week is not a lot. Teaching two classes of Chinese and also history or geography means three or four hours of classroom teaching every day, which forces them to go home with a tired body and stare at more than 100 (50 to 60 people per class is very common) half-baked papers with distress. What's more, a part-time Chinese teacher teaches even more hours than 20 hours?

Under such circumstances, it is difficult to have time to engage in research work. Their teaching content has to be pitifully poor. They have to perfunctorily deal with students and please students. Such a teacher has to be a "careless" teacher. Can we still talk about teaching efficiency here?

In order to avoid "misleading the children," I don't want to be such a teacher anymore. But society cannot give people better things to do. The knowledge sold from the university is completely useless to this society, and I have no other "specialty." For some necessity, even though I don't want to harm people in my heart, how is it possible?

Blacksmith Shop 290

— Cang Yu

About five years ago, I was introduced to this blacksmith shop. Among us, getting a job is like getting an official position for those who study.

This is where we work: on the sandy ground, piles of burning coal fire encircled by iron plates, blown by the wind from the underground air duct, the fire burns very fiercely, and the temperature also rises to a very high level. At the same time, the black coal ash and yellow coal smoke also fly up together, because there is a roof above and walls on both sides, so the air in this room is completely shrouded and occupied by this smoke and ash. When I first came to work here, it was really unbearable, because of the invasion of ash and smoke, my eyes were forced to shed tears all day long, and my nasal cavity and lungs were stimulated by strange smells, and my breathing was simply abnormal, but now it seems that I have become accustomed to it and don't feel it. When it rains, the ash and smoke can't get out, which makes people even more uncomfortable. Especially in the summer, the fierce burning of twenty or more piles of coal fire, if it is not a person who is used to it, will not only be suffocated to death but also be suffocated to death.

Like the workers in other departments, we start work at seven o'clock. We are in groups of two or three, and each group occupies a pile of coal fire and an iron stool. We first pile the crushed coal tightly, and then chisel a few holes to let the wind blow out, so that the fire can burn fiercely. Then we bury the wrought iron of what we want to make in the coal fire, clamp it with large pliers, and when it is burned to a certain color, we open the pile of coal. At this time, the heat and strange smell rush out together, and then we pour it with cold water, and the ash and smoke immediately fly up, but we don't dare to be negligent at all. We have to clamp the red-hot iron to the iron stool and hit it with a hammer, you hammer, I hammer, ding ding dang dang. After hammering it, let it cool down, and then put it back in to burn, and hammer it again after burning. This

Overseas Correspondence Network

Reno: Happy City of Divorce 291

— Mori-kun

This is an interesting story of a capitalist society. Reno, the capital of the state of Nevada in the United States, is geographically just a small metropolis in the barren western mountains, but it is a world-renowned city of divorce, just as Monaco is a world-renowned gambling country.

Judge Sirent, who had approved 20,000 divorce applications in the Reno divorce court in twelve years, said when he retired at the age of sixty-three: "Two-thirds of marriages are failed surgical operations; only divorce is the remedy."

"Come to Reno for a divorce and restore your marital happiness!"

In the United States, the laws of the 48 states are all different. Some believe that "what God has joined together, let no man separate," and the states of Sands and Carolina absolutely do not allow divorce; in the District of Columbia, divorce is allowed only in cases of adultery. Most states cite serious crimes, abandonment, abuse, etc. as grounds for divorce, and there is a necessary process of "residence period" for applying for divorce, and it is necessary to reside in a certain place for one to three years. But in the state of Nevada, divorce procedures are extremely simple.

What makes the state of Nevada famous is not the snow of Sierra Nevada (which means snowy mountains in Spanish), not the virgin forests, not the mining industry, but the convenient and rapid divorce law. Reno, together with Paris and Mexico City, is known as the three major divorce capitals in the world. At the same time, Reno is now also famous for gambling.

About seventy years ago, many people came to Reno for the mining industry, and after only six months of residence, they obtained full citizenship.

According to Nevada's divorce law, if divorce is applied for on the grounds of abandonment, neglect, or abuse, and there is no appeal, a unilateral divorce is allowed; and remarriage is allowed immediately after the divorce. This is not without reason in the United States, which likes everything to be quick. Those who want a divorce run to Reno, and after only six months of residence, they can receive the benefits of local law.

This matter began to flourish especially eleven or twelve years ago. Most of the divorce visitors are from the wealthy class, and there are always more than a thousand people every year, consuming two million yuan in gold and silver. In the eyes of this small place, it is really a considerable income.

Because most of the wealthy class come here to travel and divorce, the prosperity of gambling and dancing is also natural, but therefore, even more people come.

Later, the necessary residence period for divorce was reduced from six months to three months, so the number of visitors increased even more.

Now, comparing the number of foreign divorces after shortening the residence period with those before shortening it, we can get a general idea:

Before shortening 1925——806 cases

After shortening 1927——1,603 cases

The American economy is in recession, and the mining and railway industries are not prosperous. Many unemployed people in Reno have changed to the hotel industry, and the business is very good.

Since May 1, 1931, the three-month residence period has been changed to six weeks. As a result, the unemployed in the neighboring states of Arkansas and Idaho have come to Reno to share the waste of the rich.

Top-quality wine and top-quality song and dance always come to Reno. During the annual Independence Festival (July 4), a grand boxing match is also held. Recently, there have been 189 divorce cases in Reno every day, and each divorce case is completed in six to ten minutes.

Lawyers can earn one million yuan a year, the court 260,000 yuan a year, and public gambling halls earn one million yuan a week, or 52 million yuan a year.

Because remarriage is allowed immediately after divorce, many locals have become rich overnight. A small grocery store owner has become an opponent to a millionaire woman, and a flower girl can hook up with a celebrity.

There is also a small matter that is worth recording, that is, many wealthy people often throw their wedding rings into the Truckee River in Reno, and some unemployed people and vagrants go to the river at night to pan for rings to exchange for food.

Page 21

way back and forth, we have tasted enough coal ash and coal smoke, our arms are sore, our hands are numb, and we have sweated enough. The things we want to make are only roughly shaped after such training. Sometimes when we encounter making big things, we can use a steam-powered large iron hammer to hit, which is more labor-saving. It can be said that these things are completely hammered out by hand, because the foreman only gives us a piece of wrought iron and a model. Sometimes we also do the work of bending iron pipes. We take the part of the iron pipe that needs to be bent to burn it, burn it red, and then put it between two iron bars and bend it according to the drawing.

In addition to the eight and a half hours of work during the day, we also have to do night work. But not doing night work is something we absolutely don't want. Think about it, what can we do with seven or eight cents a day? Not doing night work will not even be able to support our families! The lower the job, the lower the wages; the lower the wages, the more we hope to do more night work. In short, we are desperately fighting with life!

The iron hammer hits day after day, and the calendar pages fly away page by page. Five years have passed quickly. During this period, I think we have hammered out a lot of things. They always create some happiness for people and earn profits for some people; but what about us? We are still "our arms are sore," "our hands are numb," and "we have sweated enough" to auction off our labor! Moreover, this blacksmith shop has now added some partners, and more piles of coal fire have been surrounded. The sound of the iron hammer is louder than before, and the coal ash and coal smoke are also denser than before.

Small monograph

Conflicts Between England and Japan in Trade 292

— Xueyou

Anyone who pays attention to recent international news will surely not overlook the recent head-to-head commercial battle between England and Japan and the complete failure of the Anglo-Japanese consultations! Here, let us try to briefly describe the beginning and end of this Anglo-Japanese commercial war.

Since abandoning the gold standard in 1931, Japan has been actively expanding its trade to the world, using the method of "devaluing the gold standard". As a result, the export trade volume in 1932 increased by 263 million yuan compared with the previous year, with a total amount of 1.41 billion yuan. In 1933, it made even greater strides, increasing by another 451 million yuan compared with 1932, with a total amount of 1.861 billion yuan. This made the British Empire, known as the world's number one trading nation, unable to help but be envious.

It wouldn't matter if Japan's trade volume was just gradually increasing. Unfortunately, one-quarter of Japan's exports are specifically sold to the UK, its autonomous territories, and colonies. In other words, in 1933, Japanese goods exported to the British Empire reached as high as 484 million yen. Among them, the goods exported to India were the most, reaching 205 million yen, almost half of the total British Empire imports from Japan.

Even more unfortunately, Britain has always dominated the world with cotton textiles, and cotton textiles have always been the main export to British autonomous territories and colonies. Japan is now competing with Britain, and the goods it exports to British autonomous territories and colonies are also centered on cotton textiles. In 1933 alone, cotton textiles exported from Japan to various British territories reached 149 million yuan (877.7 million square yards). India had the most, reaching 71.1 million yen (455.1 million square yards).

During the same period, Britain exported 485 million square yards of cotton textiles to India. This is almost equal to Japan's export volume to India.

In order to protect its own cotton textile industry and consolidate the power of the British economic bloc, Britain had to devise a way to resist Japan's fierce attacks. In August 1932, the British government incited the Indian government to revise the import tariff on cotton textiles. As a result, Japanese cotton textiles were subject to a heavy tax, increasing from 31% to 50%, while the import tax on British cotton textiles remained at 25%. In April 1933, British Foreign Secretary Simon notified the Japanese Ambassador to the UK, Matsudaira, that the Indo-Japanese Commercial Treaty concluded in 1904 would be abolished the following year. On September 25, representatives from both Japan and India gathered in Shimla, India. After half a month of meetings, no results were obtained. Later, on October 23, the meeting was moved to Delhi. After several consultations, an agreement was finally reached on January 5 this year. According to this agreement, Japan's annual export of cotton textiles to India shall not exceed 400 million square yards, and Japan must purchase 1.5 million bales of raw cotton from India each year. The import tax on Japanese cotton textiles remained at 50%.

Now that the trade dispute between Japan and India has been resolved, the next step is to negotiate the trade issue between Japan and the British Empire. On February 14 this year, the Anglo-Japanese private cotton industry conference opened in London. The representatives from both sides were all giants in their respective countries' cotton industries. After a month of negotiations, they finally broke down due to the issue of territorial application (Britain insisted that the scope of the agreement should include the markets of third countries other than England and Japan, while Japan insisted that it should be limited to the UK and its colonies). After the breakdown of the private conference, the entire issue was transferred to the governments of the two countries for resolution. After much back-and-forth consultation, no progress was made. On the 3rd of this month, British Secretary of Commerce Runciman handed a memorandum to the Japanese Ambassador to the UK, Matsudaira, and the consultations between the two governments also broke down.

With the breakdown of the consultations between the British and Japanese governments, the British government mobilized all autonomous territories and colonies to work together to exclude Japanese goods. The Anglo-Japanese commercial war has officially begun. (Recently, Australian Foreign Minister Latham went to Japan to conduct preliminary trade negotiations with Foreign Minister Hirota. Although there are no official results yet, due to Australia's relationship as a British autonomous territory, it is feared that there will be no satisfactory outcome in the future.) Although the Conservative Party of England (the most powerful force in the current cabinet) is still dreaming of the "Anglo-Japanese Alliance," the fact is already obvious: the British cotton textile industry can no longer endure Japan's attacks, and from now on, they can only engage in head-to-head commercial warfare.

Regarding the British military deployment in Singapore and various parts of Southeast Asia, the origins of the secret Anglo-Dutch meeting, and the British attitude in the voice of Japan's opposition to "international aid to China,"...we can only grasp the true meaning from the fact of this conflict between England and Japan in trade.

Amateur Studies

Studying Literature on Your Own - Some Basic Questions! 293

— Chu

(1) How to Find a Path for Research

Although our starting point for research is the actively evolving concrete literary movement, with the scope roughly limited to existing Chinese creations and translations, it is a relatively narrow field. But how should someone who is beginning to engage in research find a path for research? This is a pressing question.

Entering the study of literature through literary history, and then exploring the various branches in order according to the evolution of literature, is a research method from vertical to horizontal, and it is a good method for self-study. But here, we have many difficulties: because what is becoming our object is constantly changing literature, a complex and contradictory mixture. There is a lack of systematic opinions and decisions on this phenomenon, such as the relatively fixed opinions of past literary histories. And the path of self-study that we want to find still requires us to look for living historical materials, to diligently explore the news of literary organizations and activities, to collect historical materials such as papers, essays, criticisms, and anecdotes about the literary world from the publishing industry and various literary and non-literary publications, and to enrich our own views. From these materials, you can see the mainstreams and trends of literary activities. You can have a more accurate understanding of the complex phenomena of the present, and you will not lose your way forward. Naturally, this road that is unfolding in front of you still needs to be decided by your own will.

(2) How to Increase the Ability to Discriminate

In order to have a considerable ability to understand modern works, you should have knowledge of literary theory. To understand the works of a certain school, it is best to first read all literary theories about that school. Although theory is derived from facts, a scientific action takes the knowledge accumulated from past actions as the starting point of theory. Therefore, scientific action is guided by theory.

We should have the following basic knowledge:

1. On the theory of art

2. On literary trends of thought

3. On the social basis of literature and art

4. On aesthetics... and other more specialized research

This part of research should account for a large proportion and be the center of literary research. From this, you can complete the tasks that should be performed in the first item.

For the above aspects, it is of course possible to conduct separate specialized research.

Only when this part of the work is done sufficiently can you exert your power.

(3) Literature and Other Sciences

Literature is not an isolated thing that is unrelated to other sciences. On the contrary, it maintains appropriate and coordinated relationships with social sciences and other sciences. If you want to study literary theory, you need to have a solid foundation in social sciences and other sciences. A person who lacks research in social sciences cannot truly understand literature or be a literary scholar.

A writer, like a reader, should deeply cultivate his own foundation, and at the same time apply what he has learned to literature?

You must quickly learn the following sciences.

1. Basic knowledge of economics to understand modern society.

2. Basic knowledge of sociology to understand the course of social evolution;

3. Basic knowledge of social ideology to understand social consciousness;

4. Basic knowledge of philosophy on the scientific worldview, worldview and outlook on life.

(4) Literature and Life

Literature cannot be separated from life. To understand a modern work, even if you have the above theories, if you are separated from the practical life, you cannot grasp the center of gravity of the era, and there is a risk of becoming mechanistic or metaphysical. Therefore, a writer and a reader should understand literature in practical life.

The Original Broadcasting Station for International Broadcasting - The Soviet Union's Flax Industry 294

During the first Five-Year Plan, the area of flax cultivated land roughly doubled, which was 2.7 times greater than before the war. At the same time, in other European countries, this area has decreased by more than half (60 percent). In 1932, the Soviet Union's flax production accounted for 90 percent of the world's total production.

The massive increase in the area of flax fields is due to the social and economic changes in Soviet agriculture that laid the foundation.

As for the area of ramie cultivated land, it has now increased to 800,000 hectares (Hectares, a French land area unit), while before the war it was only 680,000 hectares.

At the beginning of the first Five-Year Plan, the main producers of flax and ramie were individual farmers (Individual Peasants). At that time (1928), the flax production of collective farms only accounted for six-thousandths of the total production. By 1932, collective farms and state-owned farms had become the main producers of flax and ramie, and their output had reached more than 65 percent of the total production.

What is particularly needed in the cultivation of flax and ramie is cultivation machine stations. In 1932, there were 261 such cultivation machine stations specifically set up for the cultivation of flax and ramie. There were 7,593 cultivators active on 500,000 hectares of flax cultivated land (one times greater than the rest of Europe) and 80,000 hectares of ramie cultivated land.

These many cultivation machine stations are all equipped with the most modern agricultural machinery. Here are the best-trained political supervisors, managers, and rural economic forces丨丨These are powerful tools for greatly increasing hemp production.

State-owned farms and collective farms (mostly in areas with cultivation machine stations) now have 15,000 well-trained flax threshing workers.

The results obtained from the effort to increase flax production are not only that the area of flax cultivated land has expanded, but also that there has been a significant increase in harvests, and the number of hemp products that can be sent to the market has naturally increased even more.

The method of purchasing hemp is now completely different from the past. Under the circumstances where market transaction prices are uncertain, the state needs to stipulate in the contract that producers (collective or individual) are given the benefit of loans and advances, and the latter supplies cotton products to the state. In these contracts, the state provides producers with necessary subsidies in production, such as providing them with agricultural machinery, mineral fertilizers, grains, selected seeds, and credit and monetary advances. At the same time, hemp producers engage in cultivating a certain amount of hemp fields, and depending on the agricultural technical consumption required for this type of cultivation, they are required to contribute a certain percentage of the high-quality harvest to the state within a certain period.

This flax loan and advance contract began to be implemented on a trial basis in 1927, and the ramie loan and advance contract began to be implemented on a trial basis in 1929. During this period, this method was only implemented on a trial basis on 9% to 14% of the cultivated land area. By 1931 and 1932, the area cultivated using this method had increased to more than 84 percent of the total hemp field.

Regarding the collection of hemp, the Soviet government has specially established a hemp industry department to manage it. Here, they often plan how to increase production and improve quality.

The task assigned to hemp producers in the first Five-Year Plan was to greatly expand the area of hemp cultivated land, and this has developed exactly as desired. The 2.3 million hectares of flax fields and 860,000 hectares of ramie fields stipulated in the 1933 plan were realized without any difficulty. Flax production increased by 20 percent in 1933, with a total production of 550,000 tons in one year.

Continued on page 5

Page 22

Page 23

After you understand the living environment of the upper social strata, you should also understand the lives of social strata different from yours. Because of the differences between social strata, there are obvious differences in internal consciousness; even in daily habits, living moods, and language, different imprints are left. How should you explore this? This is a very important and interesting question.

On the one hand, be faithful to the investigation of your own life, carefully record its truth, and clarify the characteristics of your own social stratum. Don't let up on a single point. At the same time, you should talk to people from social strata different from yours, mingle with them, and carefully understand everything about them. You should visit factories, mines, warships, schools, offices, slums, and even brothels and prisons. You should pay attention to the comedies and tragedies of life in all social strata. On the streets, in streetcars, and in theaters, you should patiently read court judgments, social news, and local communications.

All of these can provide you with rich materials and broaden your horizons.

The above is the most valuable learning of life, not only for the study of literature.

Amateur Coffee Shop

Innocent Children - The Greatest Messengers of Heaven 295

— Wang Yuehan

Children are great, so philosophers and poets throughout the ages have worshiped children.

Mencius said: "A great man does not lose the heart of a child." Jesus said: "Children are the greatest messengers of heaven." Lao Tzu said: "Focus solely and be as weak as an infant." Goethe even said: "We should take them (children) as teachers." The great thinker Marx also often said: "The place in the Christian Bible that I pay most attention to is its great love for children."

Why are children so worthy of worship? Is the worship of children just a temporary pleasure for adults? Or have adults really discovered in children the greatness that adults do not possess? Are children stronger than adults? Are their intellectual abilities superior to adults? Are their experiences and thoughts superior to adults?

To understand the true greatness of children, we cannot use ordinary people's views to measure children. We must experience the greatness of children from the children themselves. The American child psychologist Hall said: "Childhood is the heaven of mankind, and adult life is a fall from it." This is absolutely correct. All the wisdom we adults have is inseparable from slave prejudices. All my habits and all past traditions oppress the minds of us living people like nightmares. From childhood to death, adults are not free from the shackles of slavery. What qualifications do we have to comment on the personality of children?

Children, why are they great? It is because children have the innocence that adults do not have. Children cry when they want to cry, and laugh when they want to laugh. They never care about forces outside of themselves. The nature of children makes children only seek self-development and satisfaction of happiness. A child is a fearless pursuer of happiness. Children can seek comfort from adults, but they cannot easily give what they have in their hands to others. In other words, children are completely natural people who live for themselves. Children have absolutely no adult prejudices or moral concepts. This is the greatness of children.

Some people may retort: If what you say is true, then children are just selfish and self-interested creatures. What is there to be great about them, and what is there to worship? My answer is: Yes; children are indeed selfish and self-interested creatures, but this is precisely where the greatness of children lies.

What is greatness? Greatness refers to things that benefit mankind. The reason why children are great is because children are a symbol of happiness.

Everyone lives for themselves, and everyone has the instinct to pursue happiness. And when he encounters obstacles in his pursuit of happiness, he can break the obstacles without any fear. The destruction of objects that hinder him is a manifestation of this instinct. So many people say that if children had the power of adults, they would be great villains in the world.

But we adults all come from childhood. How did adults lose the nature of childhood? This cannot but be attributed to the social system of mankind. In the long-term struggle for survival, mankind has realized that sacrificing certain pleasures and desires and development is necessary, so a social system that departs from personal wishes naturally arises. The social system is to the individual as the owner of a garden is to flowers and trees. The owner always tries to make the flowers and trees lose their self-desires and development, so that they suit his own preferences. Therefore, the social system deprives people of their absolute existence, so that they no longer know themselves. Later, society not only makes its members sacrifice certain instinctive needs to satisfy certain instinctive needs, but also makes some people sacrifice instinctive needs to satisfy the unlimited needs of other people. Mankind has reached this point, just as Rousseau said:

'Except for the whole and public life, they do not know that they have themselves.'

But the need instinct and the desire for satisfaction of mankind will not be eradicated by suppression. Mankind is like a willow tree that grows upward. If you force it to bend, you can do it temporarily, but its original nature will not change, and it will still flourish upward when artificial means cannot reach it. So Gaozi said: "To use the innate nature as benevolence and righteousness is like using a willow tree to make a goblet." If mankind cannot completely lose the instinct to seek satisfaction and freedom, then children preserve the simple form of these instincts. Therefore, children become a symbol of happy mankind and are messengers of heaven. The innocence of children awakens the adult slaves who lost their instincts and desires at the entrance of civilization. Therefore, adults who feel like slaves develop respect for this great enlightenment of children.

Book and Newspaper Recommendations

Two Fairy Tales for Children to Read 296

— Jinshan

The fairy tales that Chinese children read are mostly about princes, nobles, gods, and monsters... kinds of characters. The influence of these fairy tales on children, in addition to making them imagine that they can also be in the situation of the protagonists in the fairy tales, it is very difficult to find some social and scientific knowledge to instill in children. But the few fairy tales that I have seen now, although not written by Chinese people, but translated, have completed the above requirements and are suitable for Chinese children. So I will now make a brief introduction, which can also be regarded as doing a voluntary advertisement for bookstore owners.

The first book is "Charlie Chaplin's Travels" by the new American writer Gold. The story is about a little boy, Joe, and his two older brothers, Adam and Andy, who went out for a picnic one day, but he himself was sick in bed because he ate too much ice cream. He asked to hold a race, but his mother said that the room was too small to hold it and asked him to get a good night's sleep, so he started to quarrel. But he could not resist the power of the Sandman, and slowly fell asleep. Then the clown Charlie Chaplin appeared. Charlie Chaplin very skillfully arranged a race for Joe; he took Joe to the mayor of New York to ask for permission for the race, but the mayor said that the race was too much trouble for him and refused to issue it. Charlie Chaplin then took Joe to ride an elephant to find the giant Jem丨丨He was a very kind black man who could play the "saxophone" (an American instrument). The giant Jem kindly agreed to Joe's request, climbed onto the elephant, and began to play his "saxophone". Everyone who heard him play the "saxophone" would follow him, so slowly a huge race formed. Joe was very happy in his heart. When they arrived in New York, the mayor and his police had already taken clubs and were ready to arrest them for disturbing the peace. Charlie Chaplin escaped, and Joe also escaped. The mayor chased after Joe, and Joe was so scared that he was about to cry, and woke up.

You see, isn't this an interesting fairy tale?

Another book is "The Adventures of a Young Pioneer" by the Soviet Russian Lozanov, which gives children more novel enlightenment about social and scientific aspects.

The story is of course also about a little boy, Traffoker. Once, he and his father went out to be guests. But unfortunately, his father and son were separated at the train station. So Traffoker decided to be independent and start his own life. In this way, in this book, the author tells each reader about telegraphs, train station management systems, train locomotives, signal machines, telephones, automobiles, postal telephones, public taxis, newspapers, typesetting, page layout, printing, trams, and inquiry bureaus... and also implies the socialist construction to the reader. The ending is of course that Traffoker was found by his father and mother.

Both of these books have very moving illustrations. The former is 20 cents per copy, and the latter is 50 cents per copy.

Biographies of Celebrities

Marconi, the Inventor of Wireless Telegraphy (7) 298

— Sen Ran

We know that since the Renaissance, with the development of capitalism, there have already been many great inventions in science. Leaving aside other things, just the inventions directly related to wireless telegraphy, there were many before Marconi became famous, such as the electromagnetic telegraph, generators, telephone, wired telegraph... all of which were invented before Marconi began his research. All these inventions, all the scientific and cultural heritage since the Renaissance, are the foundation for Marconi's invention of wireless telegraphy. Without this foundation, no matter how clever or persevering he was, he would not have achieved such success. Imagine, if Marconi had been born in the dark ages of the Middle Ages, could he have invented wireless telegraphy? Of course not! This is one reason.

Secondly, the era in which Marconi lived was the era of capitalism's development into imperialism. In this era, the capitalist economic network had already enveloped the entire world. Imperialist countries were striving to compete for markets to sell goods, and desperately vying for colonies. Under these circumstances, rapid transmission of information was required in commerce, military affairs, and politics. Marconi's invention of wireless telegraphy was realized under this demand. In this regard, we can say that the British naval exercises and the South African War at that time were greatly related to Marconi's success.

At the same time, the place where Marconi was born and raised also has an inseparable relationship with his invention. We know that he was born in Italy and active in Britain and America. These countries are all advanced countries, and their cultural level is above average. The so-called modern civilization is represented by them. Only in such a social environment could Marconi have the possibility of inventing wireless telegraphy. If he had been born in China or India, he would not have accomplished such a great undertaking.

In addition, Marconi's personal living environment is also very important. The issue is very obvious: if he had not been born into a wealthy family, had not received higher education, and if he had not received guidance from Professor Righi, had not been inspired by Hertz's experiments, and had not encountered Preece's help, then I dare say that no matter how great a genius he was, he would eventually be buried. As for the invention of wireless telegraphy, it would have to be left to others.

Naturally, we cannot deny Marconi's intelligence and perseverance. But this is only one factor that enabled him to become a great inventor; what made this possibility a reality was the era he lived in, society, and his personal living environment.

Finally, after evaluating Marconi, I hope that those who generally admire heroes and geniuses will not be superstitious about heroes and geniuses, but should understand them scientifically. Only in this way will we not go down a mysterious path! (The End)
